## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the stress-strain-temperature relationship for a material, which is a fundamental constitutive modeling problem in materials science and solid mechanics. Temperature typically modifies the elastic modulus and flow stress through thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (linear elasticity with linearly decreasing modulus)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (rational): sigma = c0 * epsilon * c1 / (c2 + T) (modulus decreasing with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain without temperature)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic hardening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook with homologous T: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (thermally activated modulus change)
- Voce hardening with T: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 - c4 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift model with T: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal factor)
- Polynomial with T coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * epsilon**2 (polynomial constitutive model)
- Hyperbolic sine creep: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon) (creep-type constitutive law)
- Zerilli-Armstrong BCC type: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 + c3 * exp(c4 * T) (dislocation mechanics based model)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear modulus decrease with temperature → multiplicative factor (c0 - c1*T) or (1 - T*c0) multiplying strain terms
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type exponential approach: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c0/T) or exp(c0*T) factors, reflecting thermal activation of dislocation motion
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon, T), representing initial yield before hardening
- Competing hardening and softening → Product form: (increasing function of epsilon) * (decreasing function of T), separable strain hardening and thermal softening
- Phase transition or melting effects → Sharp modulus drop near critical temperature: factor like (c0 - T)**c1 with positive exponent
- Dislocation-based hardening → Square root of strain: sigma ~ c0*sqrt(epsilon), from Taylor hardening theory
- Logarithmic rate/strain sensitivity → log(epsilon) terms appearing in flow stress expressions for rate-sensitive materials
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as ratio c0*T or (T - c1)*c2 reflecting fraction of melting temperature

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT expression is:
```

```

- First term: `61.347*epsilon*(-0.05077*T + 0.05077*278.148 + 1)` = `61.347*epsilon*(-0.05077*T + 14.122 + 1)` = `61.347*epsilon*(-0.05077*T + 15.122)`

- Second term: `98.579*epsilon^0.3178*exp(-5.949/T)`

- Third term: `2.304*epsilon^1.4503*(T - 278.148)` = `2.304*T*epsilon^1.4503 - 640.85*epsilon^1.4503`

So GT = `(-3.114*T*epsilon + 927.8*epsilon) + 98.579*epsilon^0.3178*exp(-5.949/T) + (2.304*T*epsilon^1.4503 - 640.85*epsilon^1.4503)`

**GT = T*a*epsilon + T*b*epsilon^c2 + d*epsilon + e*epsilon^c2 + f*epsilon^c5*exp(-g/T)**

where c2 ≈ 1.4503, c5 ≈ 0.3178.

1. `T*epsilon` (linear in both T and epsilon)
